B008O9V4C2|4.0|There's no way I could have given this album anything less than four stars.  Given Steely Dan's and Fagen's music in my life for going on forty years; there's no way this could ever score lower.  But five stars?  Sorry, I just can't do it.<br /><br />Overall, the album strikes me as too quiet, and slow.  And maybe droopy.  Before I even opened it, the album title and artwork had me thinking about global warming, the rise of the oceans, global catastrophe, and ultimately loss, lots of it.  At first it hit me as dark and cynical, even bitter (\\"dirge\\" kept coming to mind), but with more than 50 listens since I've gotten it (I pre-ordered, of course), this first impression has changed.<br /><br />It's the mentions of old guys, old hippies, old age, insecurity, loss of relevance and edge and stature--and a partner--due to physical and technical inadequacy.  There is some measure of happiness, with wisdom and hope in there, but it's tinged with what is likely going to be loss, not just a possibility, but more of an expectation.  Don, at a healthy 64 now cannot be blamed for exploring these issues, as they are already resonating with me at a mere 50.  It's kind of a downer.<br /><br />My favorite is \\"The Weather in My Head.\\" Some have ripped on this as a lightweight throwaway blues snoozer, but I really enjoy it.  I am very much hearing Deborah Coleman's [[ASIN:B000QMQOXY \\"My Heart Bleeds Blue\\"]] in this song, and distinct echoes of [[ASIN:B001EE4OZI \\"The Thrill Is Gone.\\"]]  I just wish the instrumental jam at the end of the song would go on for another ten minutes.<br /><br />I also enjoy \\"Miss Marlene.\\"  Honestly, this song is almost all [[ASIN:B001OB7RA0 \\"I.G.Y.\\"]]  The hook, the chorus, the horn punctuation, it's that same loping I.G.Y. shuffle.  But that's not a bad thing, not at all; I love that song (even that smarmy cover Howard Jones did).  At first I thought this song was a fun exercise in circumlocuting sexual arousal and congress, a la Michael Frank's [[ASIN:B006FXGXMA \\"Baseball,\\"]] but a dedicated listen to the lyrics shows it to be a smooth ode to failed love and its tragic consequences, with the strikes and spares filling as backstory.<br /><br />\\"I'm Not the Same Without You\\" has got me, not so much for the music but for its rhetorical composition.  What I thought initially was a defiantly whiny response to being dumped is really a testimony to all the good things flowing from the dumpage.  It gets even more positive as the song progresses, as the lucky schmuck is now becoming a superhuman.  It finally dawned on me: this breakup either has unleashed a powerful transformative force, the freedom and happiness allowing an unprecedented Olympian evolution, or it has shattered this poor dude's mind, and his litany of incredible improvement is pure delusion.  Or, he's just piling lie upon lie to cover up his agony.  The music is meh, but the story and its possible interpretations hooked me good.<br /><br />I'm not really a fan of \\"Memorabilia,\\" as the repeated word over and over just grates on me.  It's an interesting story of a guy who collects atomic test novelties and harkens back (again) to The Nightfly's [[ASIN:B001OB2IVS \\"New Frontier\\"]] and Cold War fascination with The Bomb.  I mean, when was the last time you heard a rock song referring to Pacific island nuclear testing, right down to specific shot code names?<br /><br />But alas, there is no [[ASIN:B00122KLZE \\"Godwhacker\\"]] in this album.  There is no [[ASIN:B00122B6EY \\"H Gang.\\"]] There isn't that one track that opens with that instantly hooky, perfectly produced thrum, and then just launches into a song you'll never get out of your head.  I kept listening for it, that one track, but it's not here.  The \\"Out of the Ghetto\\" cover is the one seriously up-tempo tune, but despite being a clear homage to Isaac Hayes, its archaic 70s throwback terminology relegates it to also-ran.<br /><br />Bottom line: it's a Fagen album, so I will listen to it a lot, and I'll treasure it as I have all the others, and it will grow on me in the years to come, as all of the others have.  But it's kinda slow, kinda dark and overall not really that happy, which is a bit of a disappointment, but I realize is also highly reflective of the artist, where he's been and where he's at.e it as I have all the others, and it will grow on me in the years to come, as all of the others have. B004KSQN7C|4.0|With a catalogue of seven albums to her name, Britney Spears has established herself as a solid pop artist. By now, fans know what to expect from a Britney album: catchy, fun songs and sometimes the occasional hint of something deeper. Britney is not known for her songwriting depth, yet considering the type of music she sets out to make, that is never a problem. By now, Britney has long since proven herself as capable of delivering solid pop albums. Femme Fatale proves to be no exception, showing Britney at her most confident since her well-publicized breakdown. Although she's never been known for being a powerful vocalist, Britney has mastered the ability to work within her limits to deliver strong, catchy tracks. On this release, Britney branched out more than on her previous albums to work with a wider variety of producers. For the most part, her risks paid off, with some of these new collaborators bringing out her best work. At the time of its release, Britney commented that she had put her heart and soul into the album, and stated that it was an album for the fans. Aside from a couple of missteps, the quality she delivers here certainly shows this.<br /><br />\\"Til The World Ends\\" sets the tone for the album immediately, and proves to be one of Britney's strongest recent tracks. Although the chorus is quite lacking in proper lyrics, the verses are strong. Britney sounds confident, which suits the upbeat track very well. The bridge is a particular strength. This is a brilliant start to what is commonly referred to as Britney's comeback album, and shows her at her finest. \\"Hold It Against Me\\" keeps the momentum going, and marks another of Britney's stronger singles. Co-penned by the very talented Bonnie McKee, this is an excellent dance track that once again showcases an assertive Britney. This song is masterfully crafted to allow Britney a chance to shine. Despite the powerful production, it works with Britney's delivery rather than competing with her for dominance. \\"Inside Out\\" is more of a hit-or-miss track, mostly due to the chorus. In this song, Britney half sings and half speaks the verses about having one last intimate encounter with a lover before they split up. The chorus is a little bland, however that has more to do with the production than the lyrics. The lyrical references to Britney's earliest hits are a nice touch. It's far from a bad track, however it does not live up to the standard set by the first two. \\"I Wanna Go\\", on the other hand, brings the quality back up with Britney singing about losing all her inhibitions, as well as some subtle references to her issues in the media. Some fans may dislike the stutter-y delivery of some of the lyrics, which at times sounds awkward (especially her delivery of the word \\"uncontrollably\\" just before the three-minute mark). However, overall it is another fun, catchy track although not Britney's best work.<br /><br />\\"How I Roll\\" is one of the weaker tracks, and a rare misstep for songwriter Bonnie McKee, although the sheer number of songwriters may have more to do with that. The track is generally underwhelming, with mediocre lyrics (\\"I got nine lives like a kitty cat\\"), and an even more mediocre delivery. Here, Britney attempts a softer, more breathy style of singing however it does not suit the track very well. There is also too much going on at once with the production for such an otherwise simple song, making it more distracting than anything. \\"(Drop Dead) Beautiful\\" picks things up once again, with Britney once again taking on a more confident approach. The chorus does get repetitive at times, which can be irritating. Guest rapper Sabi delivers a good verse, although the auto-tune on her part is a bit too much. This is far from Britney's best song, but it is a strong addition to the album.  \\"Seal It With a Kiss\\" is a true highlight, helmed by long-time collaborator Max Martin as well as Dr. Luke, both of whom know how to bring out Britney's best. Although the chorus is extremely simple and repetitive, it suits the song quite well, and is balanced out by the rather strong verses. The song is really made a strength by Britney's delivery. \\"Big Fat Bass\\" is another hit-or-miss track. Although it has some very strong moments throughout, the overall track is generally underwhelming. Britney holds her own quite well against will.i.am's production, however one of its biggest problems is that it drags on for far too long. Some listeners have also been put off by the lyrics, which appear to be a thinly veiled metaphor. It is not really a weak track, however it ends up being unmemorable in the long run.<br /><br />\\"Trouble for Me\\" is another of the album's less memorable tracks, although it is an enjoyable enough listen as the album plays through. Unlike other songs offered on this album, this one actually has a stronger chorus than verses. This is also one of the few songs where the auto-tuning of Britney's voice seems most apparent, largely because it is not used to create a necessary effect like it is in other tracks. This track is, at best, solid filler.  \\"Trip to Your Heart\\", on the other hand, is a risk that pays off. Britney once again takes on a softer vocal approach over a strong beat, which works incredibly well. This is an unexpected gem of the album, and showcases another side to Britney's abilities. The only weak patch of the song is when Britney starts listing \\"trip to your...\\" and naming various parts, since this gets repetitive and seems unnecessary. Luckily, that segment is quite short and listeners are quickly brought back to the strengths of the rest of the track. This is one of Britney's most creative tracks, and it works in her favour. \\"Gasoline\\" is another strong track that showcases all of Britney's strengths. Here, Britney uses gasoline as a metaphor to describe her partner setting her heart on fire. Despite being a strong track, it is not one of the more memorable songs that the album has to offer. It is certainly a welcome addition to the album, and definitely a grower. \\"Criminal\\" is another of the album's highlights, despite how songs about loving thugs or bad boys tend to sound contrived, regardless of who is singing them. Surprisingly enough, Britney manages to pull it off rather convincingly. This track once again proves how long-time collaborator Max Martin can truly get Britney to shine. This song also has a very different style compared to the rest of the album, making it a very refreshing change. Britney once again sounds confident in her delivery, which really helps to make it believable.<br /><br />The deluxe version of the album includes four bonus tracks. The first, \\"Up N Down\\", is one of the few tracks where the production almost overshadows Britney. Nevertheless, she holds her own well enough to make it a strong track that makes the deluxe worthwhile. The lyrics border on a double entendre, as they describe Britney asking a man to watch her as she dances. This is an excellent club song, and another album highlight. \\"He About to Lose Me\\" is by far the best track that this album has to offer, and it alone makes the deluxe version well worth the additional cost. This is one of the rare tracks where there do not appear to be any modifications to Britney's voice, and she actually sounds quite good. This song has Britney contemplating cheating on her boyfriend, commenting that he doesn't realize that he's about to lose her. The lyrics are quite strong, and this song shows that Britney truly can sing (albeit with limited range). \\"Selfish\\", in contrast, is one of the album's weakest offerings. Although it gets off to a strong start, it gets dragged down by the incredibly weak chorus and especially Britney's odd pronunciation of \\"selfish\\". The verses are decent enough that the song remains mostly tolerable; however with a weak bridge and even weaker chorus, it does not save the track. There is much better elsewhere on the album. Album closer \\"Don't Keep Me Waiting\\" is an out-of-place rock-tinged track that is rather mediocre all around. Britney does not quite have the voice to pull it off, and it is again the chorus that drags it down. The track does not really fit the style of the rest of the album, and was certainly not the best choice to end things with.<br /><br />Overall Mark: 4/5<br /><br />As a comeback album, Femme Fatale certainly achieves what it sets out to do. Britney sounds confident throughout, and it's evident that she enjoyed making the album. She took more risks than usual, mostly through trying different producers. Although this did not always work in her favour, it at least demonstrates an interest in expanding her sound. Britney has never been one to deviate too far from her signature sound, but she has repeatedly proven that she can make consistent, enjoyable pop albums. At this point of her career, no one expects any incredible vocal feats nor much lyrical depth, so complaints to that effect are rather pointless. Britney's albums are not artful masterpieces to be taken too seriously, nor are they the soulful, personal efforts of her contemporaries. Nonetheless, she fills the niche for music that is sheer fun, and has certainly learned how to work within her limits to deliver strong music.

The base concept also sounds rather cliche - two people from waring worlds fall in love and wish to leave their people's conflict behind and raise their forbidden newborn child in peace.<br /><br />And that classic idea is the only thing in Saga reminiscent of anything else I've come across, except that Vaughan knows that the interest to every great story grows from its characters.  The elements I mentioned above aren't the point of this unique story, and so they add to it.<br /><br />The strange worlds and grotesque forces Alana and Marko are trying to avoid are interesting and well developed, but it is the strength of the key characters who are ignoring, aiding, fighting or fleeing these horrors that makes this compelling.  The pacing is good (although this is an opening volume so there's a lot of groundwork being filled in) and despite the permiating oddness of the setting characters' actions and emotions feel genuine. Staples' art is great, doesn't shy away from disturbing images and suits the story well.<br /><br />I'll avoid further details to prevent spoilers, but overall Saga is an excellent start to what looks to be a hard-hitting, gripping tale.  Well worth a read if you can handle its approach to the subject matter.

B007HM2ZTS|4.0|I listen to classic rock and new hard rock all the time. Bands like Guns 'n Roses and Metallica are on my playlists and my current favorite radio station is Octane on Sirius. This is the first time I ever got into a rock band fronted by a woman. I tried to like bands Evanecance and Within Temptation, but it was always too whiny for me. Well, enter Halestorm. They have a unique, distinctive sound that I like for several reasons.<br /><br />First there is Arejay's maniac drumming style that's a mix of very impressive virtuoso stuff and plenty of humor. His groove makes each track interesting and never generic-sounding. There aren't many like him around, it's just pure bad-assness. I haven't met a drummer yet who hasn't been impressed by his style and chops.<br /><br />Then there's Lizzy's amazing vocal talent. She has a very impressive tonal range and a pleasant voice to listen to. She can go from silky smooth to belting and screaming. The most impressive thing about her voice is the amazing amount of face-melting power behind it. There are plenty of dude rock singers who simply can't even come close to it. Her style, power and range kinda reminds me of Sebastian Bach (the former singer of Skid Row) and that's a huge compliment. I guess that's why I like her singing style, she sings rock songs like a guy. I can't stand that whiny high-pitch girly stuff.<br /><br />The bass player and guitar player do their thing and they do it well. Most riffs are catchy and there are a couple of good guitar solos to be found. All in all it's a very tight-sounding band. Especially the opening song of the album shows off the band's mastery of their instruments. It's a fast-paced hard rock song with quick and clever riffs and hooks. The first four songs are high energy, hard-rock songs. After that the album slows down a lot with three slow and soft ballads. Two of which are on side A, and the third, \\"Break in\\" starts off side B of the record. This change of pace is a bit of a surprise,but it works. Towards the end the album ramps up again and it ends with the great anthem \\"Here's to us\\". My favorite song of the album would be \\"Miss the misery\\". My least favorite song is \\"Rock show\\".<br /><br />If there's any critique on the music to be had, it's the lyrics. It's a mixed bag, really. Sometimes they are clever and deep, but sometimes they seem they were written by a teenager. \\"Miss the misery\\" and \\"In your room\\" are for example good ones, while \\"You call me a b*tch like it's a bad thing\\" and \\"Rock show\\" are so bad it's almost awkward to listen to. I wonder why it's all over the place like that.<br /><br />Another point of critique I have is the production of the album. Like many modern albums, it's WAY too compressed and loud for it's own good. I just can't wrap my head around why producers keep doing this. Every single track on this album is clipped, yes, CLIPPED!!!!!!!, except for \\"Break in\\", which is -0.02 db from the top. It angers me that this great album could have sounded so much better if the producer didn't go with the loudness war treatment. It's just such a shame because there are so many things on this album that would benefit from some proper dynamic range, especially the drums. Instead of having that \\"blast\\"-effect, they sound flat. Everything is just LOUD with hardly any distinction. Instead of punchy and alive, the sound has that dry, flat quality to it. Their first album sounded much better, audio-quality wise. If you don't understand any of this, check out Metallica's \\"Black album\\" from 1991 to hear just how good a properly mastered rock album can sound like. Also listen to Metallica's \\"Death magnetic\\" to hear the absolute worst sounding album of all time.<br /><br />So, is this a perfect album? That answer would be \\"no\\", but that's okay. Only albums like GnR's \\"Appetite for Destruction\\" and Led Zeppelin' \\"IV\\" make that list for me. Is it a very good album? Yes, for sure. It's been quite a while since I've listened to an entire album this many times in a row.<br /><br />In fact, I liked it so much that I went out to get the vinyl version. The vinyl album sounds much more alive and dynamic than the MP3/CD. If you want the best sounding version, get the good 'ol record. Also be sure to catch them live if they stop by your town, they're an amazing live band.

B005HIBWFW|5.0|This film has so much going for it that you should stop and think twice before dismissing my claim.<br />First of all it is a genuine Tragedy in the Aristotelian sense.<br />Secondly, it is the tragedy of a major musical genius who is also a popular 'romantic artist'.<br />Thirdly, he is treated by Russell as the representative Romantic Artist who tries but fails to live up to his ideals, or, to put it another way, it's about the distance between the life and the art. This has always been Russell's main theme as a filmaker but you need to have his films about Debussy, Rossetti, Isadora Duncan, Richard Strauss and Delius, all made for BBC television, to put alongside the more familiar feature films to see this pattern as a whole.<br />It also touches profoundly, especially at the climax, on the subject of shamanism and genius.<br />Fourthly, the expressionistic visual style of the film is an attempt to create a visual equivalent of Tchaikovsky's kind of Romantic music as an art form. In this it is nothing less than an experimental arthouse film - and a successful experiment at that.<br /><br />What other film in the 'all time great' category has this sort of grand universality of subject matter including Art, genius, Tragedy, the Romantic Artist, failed ideals of the highest kind? None at all with the possible exception, stretching my categories a bit, of 'Les Enfants Du Paradis' or perhaps the Russian film of 'War And Peace'. Neither of them is British so I nominate this film as the best British feature film on the grounds of subject matter combined with its powerful treatment in what is an undoubtedly non-naturalistic and original way - sometimes even Expressionistic - stamped in every frame with the director's vision: I give points for this because it is more of a purely cinematic aesthetic than naturalism is.<br />I must admit, however, that to be fair, I should also give a very honourable mention to that other great film about Isadora Duncan called simply 'Isadora' directed by Karel Reisz and which starred Vanessa Redgrave in her finest performance. In many respects this should be considered along with 'The Music Lovers' as their style and intention is similar. It is much underrated, mainly I imagine because it isn't very well known.<br /><br />We also need to have Russell's films about Wordsworth, Coleridge, Bruckner, Vaughan Williams and Martinu, and the early one about Prokoviev, all made for television, but for ITV this time, like the missing films still not released on DVD in the UK on PAL, which I mentioned above.

1607066017|4.0|Saga, Volume 1 is a collection of the first six stories in the Saga series. Brian K. Vaughan's brilliant storytelling, backed up by the bold artistry of Fiona Staples, offers adult readers an entertaining and impressive graphic novel. As the drama unfolds, Vaughan's fans will come to appreciate the depth of the plot and the well-rounded characters that take us on a journey bursting with unexpected twists and outcomes.<br /><br />Alana and Marko's story feels like it could have been adapted from a hardcore, science-fiction version of Shakespeare's Romeo and Juliet. Alana and Marko are each from the opposing sides in an outrageous war that's expanded across the universe. Saga opens with the birth of their mixed-breed daughter; with wings from her mother and horns from her father. Aside from the opening scenes, the story is already taking a direction that show how far from ordinary it'll be. The narration sounds like it might be a third person omniscient point of view from someone with no ties to the main characters, but in reality, the narration is that of someone who is right in the middle of all the action. Hazel tells us the story of her birth and guides readers through the history of Alana and Marko's world. It was quite a surprise to recognize who the speaker is, but she bridges the story's subplots together so that the end result is smooth and tinged with chilling forewarning.<br /><br />An enormous reason why Saga drags you in and keeps you reading is because Vaughan creates a versatile dialogue. The dialogue captures each character's personality well, whether they fall along the lines of sarcastic, hateful, or pleasant. The illustrations were drawn with no limits so you never know what you might see next, but even Staples captures the danger, the tense moments, and character reactions impeccably. The characters' body language is very well in sync with their thoughts that sometimes you may not even need thought bubbles to get the sense of their next move.<br /><br />Saga is a story strictly written with an adult audience in mind. The language, the nude scenes and how the violence is depicted do not make for a story suitable for teens and younger. I thought the violence was slightly icky because you actually see the effect of someone being struck and afterwards when they're fatally injured, but it didn't completely turn me off from the story itself. I wouldn't recommend Saga to the more reserved readers or those who are relatively squeamish.<br /><br />Saga continues soon in Saga #7, and I'm so eager to see what awaits Alana and Marko. Brian K. Operating system is Kubuntu 12.04.1 64.<br /><br />First thing I noticed is ram is in more usage.  Second is when I boot Windows XP in virtualbox, this thing is about like comparing an old Charger 426 to a 318 (something many won't know about).  The boot is a matter of seconds: remember the 'puter must start up VirtualBox first, then load Windows.  Actual boot time is 23 seconds start to finish.  Some of this seems due to the processor's better utilization of hard and soft memory, including drives.  Since I don't usually use windows any longer, except for some programs, to get a better handle on speed I opened my sound lab and did a modification of some old songs that needed pops removed, volumes adjusted and so forth.  That process was near twice as fast as with the Phenom.  Also, since virtualbox supplies the platform for windows to run, there are no issues about windows recognizing either the cpu or the 64 bit system, meaning windows runs much more smoothly than by itself.  Also, this removes the security issues Microsoft has always had.<br /><br />Also, once the cpu was installed and running (BTW, linux recognized and used the potential instantly) I decided to reinstall the 64 bit version of linux.  That installation was finished much more quickly than with the Phenom, strangely enough.  Also found that downloading large files seems quicker, probably due to the faster/more efficient memory/disk operations.<br /><br />Considering the multitasking aspect, since linux is much better at that than ms, I can have a dozen iterations of windows running, but setting tasks on each at the same time I can't do because the thing finishes a task more quickly than I can start more.  So if your standard usage includes the multitasking, this is a good one.<br /><br />Other reviews complain about the noisy fan when the thing revs up; frankly, I noticed it more with the Phenom than with the 8120.  Some of this is due to the fact that next to my box is a rather large true sine UPS (2kVA, runs all the computers/printers and such) which makes substantial noise, so commenting on that would mean little: I just don't notice the fan noise much.<br /><br />As an upgrade, then, this is probably one of the best I've done re performance boost in a single easy step.

1451695195|5.0|Hollywood could not have scripted a more plausible or powerful scenario to demonstrate the existence of heaven and the afterlife than the experience of Dr. Eben Alexander. A top neurosurgeon whose whole career was focused on the brain as the seat of consciousness, he got bacterial meningitis with no history of exposure. It was such a virulent form that it put him into a coma and stopped all his higher brain functions. According to current medical understanding, he could not have been thinking or even dreaming and should have died, yet he returns to life bursting with joy at having met God.<br /><br />Having been in a deep coma for six days his doctors expected him to be a vegetable should he even survive, yet he regained his full memory and faculties. Not surprisingly, the experience forever changed his understanding of consciousness and of our place in the universe. He tried every possible medical, physiological and biochemical alternative to explain his experience, yet each one was discounted in turn, leaving only the mystery.<br />I am reminded of the TV ad with the cell phone testers asking, \\"Can you hear me now?\\"<br /><br />As a radio host and reviewer I have received a surprisingly large number of books describing near death experiences, each one offering similar or complementary insights about the nature of death and divinity. One of the reasons this book stands out is that Dr. Alexander's credentials are unassailable, the case was impeccably documented, and he was a skeptic with no ax to grind for a divine or metaphysical explanation. We are also given enough of the scientific details to understand what a miracle this truly was.<br /><br />The book is beautifully written, and deftly interweaves his personal story with the drama of his illness, recovery and attempts to understand what happened. THIS WILL BE THE LAST WARNING.<br /><br />Anne's defining moment is her refusal to katow to her sister Isabel and the sister's husband George of Clarence.  Anne demands a share of their mother's inheritance, but rather than heroic defiance, it seems scaled smaller--one sister saying to another, you cannot have everything. The sibling rivalry seems petty and commonplace given the way the two have stood by each other earlier.<br /><br />The book becomes claustrophobically frustrating with each page after the first two thirds. She has been depicted as in love with Richard, and now we doubt that he ever loved her.  Was it all as her mother maliciously insists, a ruse to be able to divorce her when it suits his purposes?  Can it be that he is plotting to marry a younger woman, now that they have arrived upon the throne?  This book's Anne never confronts him about this, just as she never brings up the matter of obtaining a dispensation to fully legalize their marriage. The reader may suspect he is poisoning her to death instead of taking the divorce route because it grows naturally from what we are seeing, but Anne never makes this explicit. There is only so much we can see from her eyes, and we feel as the book closes, that she is willing herself to blindness.<br /><br />It might have happened this way, but the story as told seems flat and narrow. At the end, I feel less a sense of illumination than merely glad that it's over.  The simple first person POV also presents her state of mind redundantly, and while this may be accurate in the way people tend to repeat things, it also makes the novel boring.

0761171703|5.0|For anyone who doesn't already know his work (and he's been a New York treasure for years), this book is a perfect introduction to photographer Jordan Matter--an artist who is equal parts technical master, thoughtful witness, and great lover of mischief. Both his books, Uncovered and now Dancers Among Us, have involved high-risk shoots that probably should have gotten him in some form of trouble, even when they didn't. But a general disinterest in permission is the brand of any self-respecting auteur, and Matter comes away with photographs so remarkably unique, it's just too easy to enjoy him.<br /><br />This book in particular is a portrait of the photographer as much as his subjects. Yes, there are pages upon pages of gorgeous, virtuosic dancers doing incredible things in unexpected spaces--from lovers kissing upside down under the Santa Monica Pier as the tide rolls in, to a pickaxe-wielding farmhand leaping to his chores like a gazelle, his body suspended some 10 feet off the ground. There are charming guest appearances by performance legends Bill Irwin and Bebe Neuwirth (both seemingly ageless). But they're framed by intimate stories from Matter himself--reflections on his youth, his wife, his children and his own journey from aspiring athlete to creative photographer, from rootless youth to proud husband and father. These stories establish the book's many quotations (from Mae West, Edith Wharton, Samuel Beckett and others) as expressions of the artist's own spiritual compass. Through words, they present a path toward welcoming the essence of a dancer in ecstatic motion into our own souls.<br /><br />Make no mistake, the beauty and athleticism in Dancers Among Us is jaw-dropping. The narratives these images create, in an instant, are delightful. Many locations are stunning (and clear evidence of one epic road trip). But as both his published works demonstrate, Matter is no coffee table book photographer. We don't just see, we're asked to think, and reflect, andappreciate--and think again. Matter's images always come contextualized with stories. It turns out his are as wonderful as anyone else's.

0575095830|4.0|ANALYSIS: To say this book was highly anticipated would be an understatement, once it was announced that this book would be featuring the return of Logen Ninefingers. A character that has been synonymous with the term \\"bad-ass\\" along with other famous ones such as Druss, Anomander Rake, Waylander, Oberyn Martell etc.<br /><br />After reading the ending to the First Law trilogy, many readers were left stymied a bit with it. Most characters had an ending that belied their start however for one particular character the journey was a full circle. People were left wondering what exactly happened to Ninefingers and this book answers the pivotal question of his survival without divulging any particular details as to how. The following review will have some minor spoilers for the previous five books and for this one so be warned for those who haven't read all the previous titles.<br /><br />The story begins in a bloody fashion of sorts wherein we are introduced to the main protagonists Shy South and Temple. Shy is a person who has had a rough adolescence and is now learning to live straight. She has her stepfather Lamb to help her out however with his timid behavior it often turns out that she has to step in to take care of situations as they arise. Temple is a jack-of-many-trades, who considers himself a coward of the highest order and is currently working as the legal counsel to Nicomo Cosca and his band of mercenaries.<br /><br />Both characters have a journey ahead of them thanks to the actions of others and this is where this fantasy western story really explores the arc of each and every character. The story is focused on Shy & Lamb's search for Ro & Pit, the two missing children who have been abducted along with a host of others by an outlaw called Grega Cantliss. Their search however will cross roads with Nicomo Cosca and his band of mercenaries that include Temple and sergeant Friendly (seen previously in Best Served Cold).  Cosca is going along with the inquisition to root out the rebels and is actively searching for a specific rebel leader.<br /><br />For me this book was the best of Joe's standalone books and possibly one, that is great for all those wanting to see and read more about Ninefingers as he returns in a bloody manner as befitting his nature. The story follows a couple of plot threads that start divergently but soon merge in a surprising way that makes the book slightly more streamlined.  Shy South and Temple can be said to be the main POV characters among the various ones featured in the book; however the sad part is that we don't get a POV from the character that we want to know about the most.<br /><br />This part seriously was the biggest downer of the story for me as with everyone else I wanted to know about Logen and what he had been doing after his betrayal by Black Dow. We never get a clear cut idea about whether his so-called berserker state is super-natural or just a part of his mental persona. The author certainly loses points for this move as to not feature Ninefingers as a POV robs the story mightily of its sheen.<br /><br />The pacing of the story however is spot on and we get a story that is a western as well as a redemption tale. The character arcs explored are very similar to a Stephen King story wherein flawed characters either make it or they don't but their journey will be one that enthralls the readers and powers the story completely. Plus Logen Ninefingers finally transcends his journey into an iconic one by accepting who he is and what he is not, hopefully the author might provide further illumination by featuring him in more stories.<br /><br />I was waiting to know all and be enchanted by Logen's presence in the book but to paraphrase Logen himself \\"you have to be realistic about these things.\\" The ending of Red Country is perhaps much more optimistic than of the First Law trilogy and for that I'm glad however it is still as open ended as its predecessor and that might be a sticky pointfor some. I loved this book and the way the story ends readers will be hoping that we get to know more about what happens next for several characters.<br /><br />Joe Abercrombie definitely knows how to write a story, he also knows to create memorable characters but his strongest suit is his dialogue and writing copious amounts of black humor. This book is no stranger to these facts and it manages to be the most uplifting of all his standalone books by virtue of twists and turns of this story. The book is a complete winner for all fans waiting for the return of one of the most iconic barbarians ever, however for fans wanting to know Logen's inner thoughts they might just have to wait a little longer. Dive in to read another fantastic effort by a veritable fantasy writer who is the first law when it comes to writing dark, bloody, action packed stories.for some. B009AJDDQU|2.0|I will avoid a distillation of my philosophical and theological misgivings with \\"Prometheus.\\" All I will just say is that the film is a scientistic reiteration of Gnostic creatology laced with misotheism. Such an interpretation of our origins disagrees with my own outlook. Moreover, it is a stale hypothesis that creates more questions than it answers. That aside, I think that \\"Prometheus\\" also falls short in terms of storytelling.<br /><br />Yes, the film is replete with dazzling visuals and vibrant colors. My heart was gladdened by Ridley Scott's rediscovery of these elements. They were the very same elements that highlighted films like \\"Legend,\\" \\"Bladerunner,\\" and the magisterial \\"1492: Conquest of Paradise.\\" In recent years, Scott has eschewed such breathtaking visual elements in favor of an earthier, visceral style (e.g., \\"Kingdom of Heaven,\\" \\"Body of Lies,\\" \\"Gladiator\\"). To see Scott return to his former aesthetic sensibilities was, in my view, a welcome development.<br /><br />However, Scott's storytelling style has plunged into the very sort of incoherence that epitomizes the short attention span film-making approach of 21st century Hollywood. In contradistinction to most of Scott's early work, which was slower and thoughtful, \\"Prometheus\\" exhibits a ravenously kinetic narrative thrust that allows audiences little or no time to contemplate the ideas being presented to them. In fact, one could convincingly argue that some viewers might miss the ideas all together. This is unfortunate because the film's themes (human origins, exotheology, faith, etc.) should be pondered a little more thoughtfully. Yet, how can one do so when the story unfolds with such rapidity and the questions are only marginally broached by the characters themselves?<br /><br />In short, \\"Prometheus\\" represents a very gifted film-maker's conformance to the modern Hollywood formula... Placate audiences with bread and circuses. Serious thought be damned!

0385340990|3.0|In general, it is difficult to craft flesh and blood passionate characters through the technique of the epistolary novel. The viewpoints depicted are often one-dimensional as letters are usually written to make an announcement, get to a point, perhaps make a request or relate some above-average event.  Although I believe that one's voice can be revealed through letters, I do not think that the characters of Mary Ann Shaffer and Annie Barrows in their The Guernsey Literary and Potato Peel Society present themselves as thoroughly and as intimately through descriptions of their demeanor and actions as they could have been showcased in a novel written in a third person narration.<br /><br />But then again, Potato Peel Society is meant to be an upbeat little story that intertwines a dark hour in the world's history with the universal hope of being human.  The letters as the only real form of distance communication must be viewed as heraldic newsletters where the writers have already survived the events and are now reporting the past in terms of their triumph as examples of what it means to healthily \\"move on\\" and not wallow.<br /><br />Viewing Potato Peel Society in this sense works.  We become members of a private club of islanders who in their isolation during the German occupation of WW2 must devise a way to get through the every day of hunger, anger, defeat and despair.  They do--some do it better than others--and we, as readers, hear of it all in the form of stories as related to the lead character and letter writer, Ms Juliet Ashton, a column journalist for a London newspaper who is at a crossroads with regard to the rest of her life.<br /><br />Shaffer and Barrows do write with a love of literature; they quite rightly focus on what the thoughts of writers might mean to people who have no other outlet.  How many times have you read a book and then read over the writer's words and wondered at how that person could convey the emotion that you yourself were feeling or had felt at some key point in your life?  The great surge of universality does wash over you and you do feel the power of the pen and connectivity on an Absolute level far stronger than some of the senseless pings and narcissistic announcements of Facebook.  Shaffer and Barrows most ashamedly pull out all the romanticized stops--their situations are most definitely contrived and meant as English student teaching points for the reader who has little need to ponder metaphor.  An unhappier reality does intervene in the form of concentration camps, needless deaths, children separated from their families, hunger, desolation, arrests and cruelty which, at times does seem bleak in the face of all the cheery letters bandied back and forth.<br /><br />Nevertheless, Juliet as the eternal and feisty optimist does become enchanted with her collection of islanders and quite predictably opts to take on the role of more than just an honorary member of the Society.  The authors take advantage of many of the situation comedies of the 40's cinema to contrive an extravagantly outcome for all involved in tone with their theme of love and hope arising from the ashes of the Blitz, the desolation of the work camp and the frustration of being captured on your home turf.<br /><br />Bottom line?  In \\"The Guernsey Literary and Potato Peel Pie Society,\\" authors Mary Ann Shaffer and Annie Barrows strive to craft an epistolary novel that depicts the seriousness of the plight of the island of Guernsey during the German Occupation of WW2 while lauding its residents' obvious patriotism and steadfastness in the face of hardship and great adversity.  At times, the seemingly contrived naivety of main character Juliet despite her orphaned past might frustrate some looking for more depth, but for those desiring an entertainment read with some hard facts that do not diminish the overall joy of the story, a serving of Potato Peel Pie might make the perfect dessert. Recommended.<br />Diana Faillace Von Behren<br />\\"reneofc\\"hren<br />\\"reneofc\\"

B006PTL1GC|3.0|*** This review may contain spoilers ***<br /><br />'A Dangerous Method' is advertised as a film mainly dramatizing the conflict between iconic therapists Carl Jung and his one-time mentor, Sigmund Freud. But the bulk of the film is really about an affair that Jung had with one of his patients, Sabina Spielrein, who later went on to become a prominent Russian physician and psychoanalyst.<br /><br />The film begins in 1904 with Spielrein, a young medical student, checking into a psychiatric clinic with severe symptoms of what was termed 'hysteria' in those days. She primarily displays a complex motor tic of continuously thrusting her jaw out and stuttering and often must be restrained by the staff at the clinic. Carl Jung, a student of Sigmund Freud, employs Freud's new 'talking therapy' with Spielrein, who makes remarkable progress and is soon offered a job by Jung, to assist him in his medical research (Spielrein's transformation from borderline psychotic to responsible student is too abrupt as we never see how Jung actually works his miracle--Jung returns from military leave and we must take it on faith that somehow, through the passage of time, his therapy simply worked!)<br /><br />Jung is married to a wealthy woman who he has a number of children with. During the course of his relationship with Spielrein, he treats a disaffected physician, Otto Gross, who urges him to abandon his monogamous ways and pursue his sexual desires with Sabina. It is the contention of the film's scenarists that Jung indeed began an affair with Spielrein; her illness was related to being physically punished by her father in childhood and she now sublimates these negative experiences by engaging in masochistic spanking and bondage sessions with Jung (coupled with normal sexual encounters).<br /><br />Meanwhile, Jung corresponds with Freud and meets with him a number of times, including a trip to America. Freud is depicted as a rigid theoretician and practitioner, inflexibly adhering to his core belief that mental illness is rooted only in childhood sexual experiences. Jung eventually seeks to incorporate other theories to explain psychological dysfunction which Freud derides, and ultimately rejects, as 'mysticism'.<br /><br />The dissolution of Jung and Freud's relationship is tied to Jung's dissolving relationship with Spielrein. He not only publishes studies about his treatment of her but her dissertation as well. They both agree that acts of creation can be rooted in destruction (holding up their own relationship as a perfect example: a clash of opposites and breaking of taboos), not necessarily related to Freud's one note obsession with childhood sexuality. Although Spielrein is essentially on Jung's side, she decides to undergo analysis with Freud who she hopes might play mediator between the warring couple, after Jung (due to guilt feelings) breaks things off between them. While Spielrein takes the high road by not exposing Jung, she insists he confess his indiscretions to Freud. After agreeing to Spielrein's request, Freud uses Jung's confession against him, bashing Jung in future correspondence, after his former pupil fails to pay homage to him. After they split, both Freud and Jung then fail to acknowledge Speilrein's contributions. She finally gets over Jung, becomes a notable analyst in her own right and has children with a kindly physician from her native Russia.<br /><br />The resolution of both of these plot strands (Jung and Freud and Jung and Spielrein), will prove of great interest to aficionados of the great psychotherapeutic icons, but to the general public, perhaps much more anti-climactic. If we are to believe the scenarists here, Jung went way beyond his mentor Freud, in terms of presenting much broader, holistic, psychological constructs. Much of this we learn in the closing titles at film's end but I'm not convinced that Jung is the better of the two.<br /><br />To their credit, Freud is depicted as a minority practitioner,beleaguered on many sides, due to his unpopular emphasis on sexuality. He argued that Jung's belief in 'superstition' undermined the 'scientific' basis of their profession. Ultimately, a one hour and forty five minute film, can only touch upon the basic conflicting points between the two men. For a deeper understanding between Freud and Jung, a real solution is to read through their writings. Creative luminaries such as Joyce Joyce, however, did not care to--he dubbed them both \\"Tweedledum and Tweedledee\\" (perhaps if both of them had written a novel as good as 'Ulysses', they may have earned Joyce's approbation).<br /><br />Michael Fassbender as Jung is perhaps the strongest of the three principals. He displays a subdued intensity throughout the film. Many internet posters found Keira Knightley as Spielrein to be way over the top, particularly in the early scenes where she is depicted as being completely unhinged. I didn't think she was that bad at all and is perhaps the strongest when she makes her case for Jung, while meeting up with Freud. Viggo Mortensen comes off as a bit boring as Freud but is perhaps saddled by the rather ponderous, dialogue heavy script.<br /><br />'A Dangerous Method' will keep your interest up to a point. Ultimately, however, Freud and Jung's work may not be worth immortalizing in any film at all. There is a deeper and darker tale here, far more ominous and important than the conflict between seemingly self-involved intellectuals. I'm referring to the fate of Sabina Spielrein, revealed in the closing credits. She was murdered along with her two children by Einsatzgruppe D, one of the Nazi death squads, near her home town in Russia, in August of 1942. The machinations of Freud and Jung seem like a distant memory in light of the evil which inexorably began its march over the European continent some 100 years ago, almost to this day.beleaguered on many sides, due to his unpopular emphasis on sexuality. B00275EGX8|3.0|I bought this movie on DVD recently because of the hype critics gave it and it winning best picture at the Oscars. I thought it would be a great movie because it dealt with the Iraq War and I was indeed very eager to watch it. I admit I was entertained because it has some very gripping and high tension moments. All the bomb diffusion scenes and the sniper scene at the mid point were very detailed and well executed. That being said however I can't help but agree with many of the user comments pointing out the inaccuracies.<br /><br />-The opening scene has a man detonating the bomb with a cell phone and the team simply yells at him to put it down, had it been in real life the man would have been shot instantly.<br /><br />-The character Sargent First Class William James is portrayed as a rugged, careless lone wolf who ignores his teammates and at one point leaves his base to track down who he suspects killed a small boy he befriended. Had someone done these things in real life he would have been highly disciplined and more than likely discharged.<br /><br />-And the last thing I have a problem with the movie clichs soldiers as war junkies who love combat and are unable to adjust to civilian life once they return home. While some military personnel may indeed go through this, most people would be glad to be out of the war and be back home with their loved ones.<br /><br />So to sum it all up the acting was indeed very good, all the actors gave great performances and it does have high tension scenes. But if you decide to view this movie just remember it isn't a very accurate depiction of the Iraq War and most soldiers are not like the characters portrayed in the movie.

Since I want to keep the longevity of my APU, I have decided not to OC the processor and run it that way 24/7. The 200mhz boost received allows me to play even Skyrim at medium-high settings without lag. Getting both my processor and graphics card capable of running anything that I want to play for only $87 was the best deal I could ever get. Definitely recommend this for cheap gaming rigs. ^^

0061474355|4.0|If you're in the mood for a somber, gorgeously visual novel that's part Philip Pullman, part Tolkien, and part a world out of one those artful fantasy illustrations that seemed to have had a heyday in the 1970s, Sabriel might fit the bill. The heroine of the title is a girl of mysterious origins who was born in the magical \\"Old Kingdom\\" and possesses a rare natural gift for necromancy. However, Sabriel has spent most of her life in Ancelstierre, a non-magical country that resembles Britain of the early 1900s, but shares a strange border region with the Old Kingdom. The story begins with its heroine, who is completing a clandestine education in magic, learning that her often-absent father, who spends most of his time in the Old Kingdom, has gone missing. Meanwhile, the undead ghouls and spirits that plague that region have been acting up, for reasons that Sabriel doesn't understand, having been away from home for so long.<br /><br />While the quest that ensues follows a well-worn good-versus-darkness script and Sabriel herself isn't the most deeply-developed character, I enjoyed its world creation. Many of Nix's ideas, from the militarized zone between Ancelstierre and the Old Kingdom, to the different bells that perform different kinds of necromantic magic, to the beautifully eerie World of the Dead, a Stygian realm populated by beings and souls that have not yet passed entirely from life (and a third parallel reality in the story), are deliciously realized. I also enjoyed the side characters, a sardonic, semi-helpful creature of unclear origins named Mogget, who is trapped inside a cat's body, and a stolid, brooding young man named Touchstone, who is wrapped up in his own past.<br /><br />The writing resembles Pullman's The Golden Compass in that it takes its dark reality seriously and contains a few \\"adult\\" things, such as some glancing references to sex and several grim scenes of death. There's nothing I'd consider prurient or inappropriate for the average 12-13 year old, though. For my money, The Golden Compass was more interesting, but readers looking for a work like it, albeit with a more traditional sensibility, would probably enjoy Sabriel.<br /><br />Tim Curry's audiobook performance, which is a touch campfire tale and a touch Shakespearean theatre, fits the tone delightfully.<br /><br />3.5 starsyear old, though. 1400069289|5.0|What an intriguing subject matter. Often, when we think of habits, we generally think of what route we drive to work, how we dress, or how we perform even the most mundane daily tasks or worse. Charles Duhigg, in his must read treatment of the topic, has us see habits as far more intricate patterns of action. From addictions, such alcoholism, athletic practice routines that lead teams to the ultimate sports success, to corporate training curriculum that help create exceptional performing employees, and even to even shopping patterns, Duhigg demonstrates the crucial role that habits play in all parts of our life. A habit is defined early in his work as a choice that we, at some point, deliberately make, then, generally without realizing it, stop thinking about it but continue doing, often on a daily basis. The habit loop, as it he calls it, starts with the cue, such as a moment, an event or thought or such, that triggers a routine, followed by a reward of some sort that is repeated. The key to making our habits work for us and not against us is in this loop and how we learn to use it. The take away for me is that, habits can be replaced, not changed and that for even some of the most challenging and destructive patterns we find in life, if we recognize what triggers or cues exist, anything can change, which means there is still hope for me.<br /><br />I read this book as part of the 12 Books Group and encourage you to get the book and read it. You will certainly enjoy it, and who knows what lurking habits you will discover and replace.

This work, its prequel and its sequel are included in the omnibus edition [[ASIN:1416555471 Miles In Love]].  The initial work in this series is [[ASIN:0671655744 Shards of Honor]].<br /><br />In the previous volume, Miles was working with Vorthys on oversight of a serious incident in the Komarr system.  An ore freighter had collided with a space mirror over Komarr.  The mirror satellite had provided extra insolation to the planet for its terraforming.<br /><br />The satellite damage was starting to adversely effect the transplanted biology on the planet.  The Komarrans wanted the satellite fixed as soon as possible.  It was becoming a political issue on Barrayar as well as on Komarr.  Gregor wanted Vorthys and Miles to determine if the incident resulted from sabotage.<br /><br />After arriving in the Komarr system, Professor Vorthys and Miles first observed the efforts of the probable-cause team.  Then they went down to the planet to find quarters.  Ekaterin invited them to move in with them.<br /><br />Ekaterin ordered a grav bed for Miles and then prepared dinner for the Lord Auditors and her family.  Tien was very cynical about the mutant Lord Auditor and Ekaterin wondered how he obtained his injuries.  Nikki had a number of ship models and was very pleased to learn that Miles has traveled aboard many of those ships.<br /><br />In this novel, Miles Naismith Vorkosigan is the son of Aral and Cordelia.  He no longer has fragile bones;  they have all been replaced with synthetics.  He has resigned from the Barrayaran Imperial Service and now is an Imperial Auditor.<br /><br />Gregor Vorbarra is the Emperor of Barrayar.  After the death of his mother -- Princess Karenn -- he was raised by Miles' father, the Regent.  Gregor is engaged to marry Laisa, a woman from Komarr.<br /><br />Ivan Vorpatril is a Captain in the Imperial Service.  He and Miles have thesame great-grandfather;  their grandmothers were sisters.  Unlike Miles, Ivan is tall, handsome and charming.<br /><br />Alys Vorpatril is the mother of Ivan and the widow of his father.  She is a friend of Miles' mother and the official party organizer for Gregor.  She is trying to marry off Ivan and have grandchildren.<br /><br />Georg Vorthys is a retired Professor of Engineering Failure Analysis at the Imperial University of Barrayar.  He is also an Imperial Auditor and is Ekaterin's uncle.<br /><br />Ekaterin Nile Vorsoisson is a Barrayaran from the South continent.  Kat was married to Etienne -- now deceased -- and is the mother of Nikki.<br /><br />Nikolai Vorsoisson is the son of Etienne and Kat Vorsoisson.  He is very enthused about spacecraft.<br /><br />Mark Pierre Vorkosigan is a clone of Miles.  He was created by House Bharaputra of Jackson Whole for Komarr separatists.  He impersonated Miles until caught, but was freed to find his own destiny.<br /><br />Kareen Koudelka is the youngest of four sisters.  Her father had been an aide of Count Vorkosigan during the Regency and her mother has been a bodyguard of the Countess and then of the young Emperor.<br /><br />Enrique Borgos is an Escobaran genetic entomologist.  He has developed a new breed called butter bugs.<br /><br />In this story, Gregor and Laisa are to be married at Midsummer.  Everybody is talking about the wedding.  Alys, Ivan and Miles are working on the preparations.<br /><br />Miles will be Gregor's Second in the ceremony.  Alys is charged with the planning and direction of the ceremony.  Ivan is performing odd jobs for his mother.<br /><br />Miles is trying to arrange a marriage of his own.  He has fallen in love with Ekaterin, but realizes that she still hasn't recovered from her former marriage.  So he is getting involved in her life, but laying off marriage proposals.<br /><br />Miles has some competition for Ekaterin.  Ivan is attracted toward her, but he definitely is not ready formarriage.  Miles gets him to swear on his name that he will not court Ekaterin.  Yet Ivan is a bit peeved at going that far and gets a coworker interested in pursuing the woman.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Alys is issuing tasks to Miles and Ivan.  She even has ImpSec involved for the security aspects.  The wedding will be the prime event of this generation.<br /><br />Then Kareen comes to Barrayar.  She has been living with Mark on Beta Colony and doesn't quite fit the same with her family.  She is waiting for Mark to return.<br /><br />This tale brings Mark back to Barrayar.  He has brought Enrique with him as a business partner.  Kareen soon starts spending time with Mark.<br /><br />Miles plays Barrayaran politics in this story.  The next installments in this sequence are the novella \\"Winter Gifts\\" from [[ASIN:0451217241 Irresistible Forces]] and [[ASIN:0743436121 Diplomatic Immunity]].<br /><br />Highly recommended for Bujold fans and for anyone else who enjoys tales of imperial weddings, political intrigue, and tangled romance. Ishmael Beah's memoir lets us see the life of a boy soldier in 1990's Sierra Leone. If we expect nobility and dignity of warriors, A Long Way Gone describes the savage, gleeful resourcefulness of children who delight in slitting throats, playing Rambo with live ammunition, torching villages and stalking enemies. Fueled by inexhaustible supplies of drugs and ammunition, these modern day berserks are controlled and directed by adults; and because there is an inexhaustible supply of expendable children, they are used as scouts and vanguards of military operations.<br />Some of the children survive to adulthood. Some become ruthless, canny adults who wreak even more clever horror on the civilized world. Stripped of empathy and compassion, their only pleasure is mayhem.<br />Some few find healing, as did Mr. Beah. Given the opportunity to escape the inferno of war, he has begun to pursue the life of peace. This book is no doubt a part of his therapy. Although he will probably suffer nightmares and flashbacks until the day he dies, he has set out to define himself as a world citizen and peacemaker.<br /><br />Americans cultivate romantic notions about children: their innocence, beauty, naivete and vulnerability. We should put that romantic impulse to good use and invest our energies in something other than weapons and drugs. If more people read A Long Way Gone we might develop ways to invite African people to join us in building a prosperous world where children are honored as images of God.

B008JFC6F0|4.0|I can't decide which album I like better, this or Innerspeaker. Where as Innerspeaker, I feel, focuses more on the sweeping spectacle of the effects pumped into the production, Lonerism is a much more relaxed album. Its still saturated with psychedilia and can get quite loud at times, the drums and effects keep the album from stalling, but this time the beautiful relaxed voice and melodies of Kevin Parker stand out. His voice is gorgeous on this album. He makes it reeeaal difficult to not sing along with him sometimes, even if the words are sometimes hard to understand. There are layers upon layers upon layers of effects and distortion, and it often sounds rich and sharp, but sometimes muddy, although I think that was done on purpose, giving a sort of a digital fuzz to counter the sharp futuristic sounds. As I said before, Jay Walker's drumming drives the album. It reminds me of the chaotic style of a lot of 60's psychedelia combined with a repetitive loop on a drum machine. The album title definitely fits the lyrical content. There seems to be a continuous theme of not fitting in, being unsure about one's self and the future, being uncomfortable with success. I guess that's why this album feels more drawn in than Innerspeaker. Here is what I think are the stand out songs...<br /><br />\\"Be Above It\\" is a great segway from Innerspeaker, with a pounding drumline and a repetitive melody, great intro.<br /><br />\\"Mind Mischief\\" is where this album really starts to shine. Its a very laid back song, but the drums drive it. Kevin's voice shines in this, the melodies ooze like caramel and the outro gives you the feeling of floating in a soft purple haze, its probably my favorite song on the album.<br /><br />\\"Why Won't They Talk To Me?\\" has an infectious outro thats great to sing along too.<br /><br />\\"Keep On Lying\\" fades into a solemn yet driving intro, and then goes into Magical Mystery Tour/Yellow Submarine-like sound effects. It's a great example of how this band likesto smooth into these long musical tangents halfway through. The song structures aren't exactly conventional, but thats not necessarily bad. The songs are still tight. There are too many bands that go way too over-board with their talents and effects and solos, and the result is often a bloated and self-indulgent mess. Not with this album, theres just enough chaos to keep things interesting.<br /><br />\\"Elephant\\" is the albums single, and it sounds like it. It definitely sounds like it belongs on Innerspeaker, being the most outgoing and loud song on the album.<br /><br />\\"Nothing That Has Happened So Far Has Been Anything We Could Control\\" basically summarizes the sound of the album. Great high notes sung by Kevin, loud, crashing drums, waves of non-stop sound, great song.<br /><br />In short, buy this album.

160774273X|5.0|This is probably the most useful of the many excellent bread books I've read, particularly for the serious beginner -- and also for the experienced home baker.  But other reviewers have said all that, so here is my contribution to the discussion:<br /><br />If you don't already have a cast iron pot, which Forkish recommends for all of his bread recipes, consider instead getting a Sassafras LaCloche, a ceramic baking \\"oven.\\"  The down side is that ceramic breaks, and I've broken a couple over the years myself.  But by substituting a cloche for a cast iron pot, you get a miniature oven with a bell-shaped top and a shallow bottom that allows you more safely and easily to place your loaf in a 500 degree oven.<br /><br />I've tried both, using a peel to gently deposit the risen loaf on the LaCloche, which eliminates the stress associated with placing it by hand in a red-hot pot.  Removal is also easy and worry-free with the LaCloche.  And there is less danger of the dough deflating than if you drop it too hard into a hot iron pot.<br /><br />If there is a down-side, it may be that the loaf will spread out more in the LaCloche.  But if your loaf has been properly prepared and proofed, according to Forkish's instructions, and raised in a banneton or equivalent, it should hold it's shape once in the oven.<br /><br />Although iron and ceramic have different thermal characteristics, the results from both are excellent.  (Disclaimer:  I have no connection with Sassafras except as a customer.)<br /><br />By the way, the iBooks version of this book is extremely useful and convenient, especially because you can copy recipes and instructions, email them to yourself, and then edit and print them out for your personal recipe book.
